### Post by labinnsw on 2010-02-28
Never wanted the honor but, it has been 42 mins since March started in New Zealand

Rules:

1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. when possible we request that you format your posts in the following order: NOTE  this is optional

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-01
> **konqueror7 said:**
> details please? :D
*Well* I'll try... It's Openbox with tint2 of course, The theme (GTK+Openbox) was supposed to be compact-Murrine-Wisteria, but today I realized it had inherited the colours from the elementary-compact theme I used previously (and I was wondering what was wrong with it and why it wouldn't pair with its openbox theme) and the icons are AnyColourYouLike, colour #141414, Wallpaper was attached a couple of pages ago, and the fonts are Aller 8 everywhere, Terminus 10 in the terminal, and Some leftover Sansation 8 in some points.

If you need something more specific go ahead and ask :)
> **gutterslob said:**
> That has got to be one of the best wallpapers in existence!! What's amazing is that it's only a combination of an "auto" bitmap trace, some iWarp Gimp effects and gradients.... Brilliant!!
Oh, and your theme work isn't half-bad either.... only thing I'd change is the gaps in the tint2... The pink in the active-window sorta makes me curious about the look of the OBmenu (try to include it in your screenshots in future) :)

I need to hand-edit that obt to make one that's a big more grayscale. Tint2 in general needs a lot of things. Different colours and paddings in everything, disabled icons, etc etc, which I'll do today.

I'm wondering why you didn't criticize the fact that I have icons on the desktop. :P :D

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-03-01
> **gymophett said:**
> What fonts are those BTW?

EDIT: And icons?

Lucida MAC, LucidaMacBold, Monaco and Eikon2. See the instructions file.

Edit: Faceplam, I forgot to include my userChrome.css for Firefox/Thunderbird:
```
#nav-bar
{
	border: none !important;
	padding: 0px !important;
}

menubutton, menulist, menu, menuitem
{
	font-family: LucidaMacBold !important;
	font-size: 8pt !important;
}

menubar
{
	min-height: 12px !important;
}

/*make the menubar use gray color for text*/
menubar > menu
{
	color: #afafb5  !important;
	font-family: Lucida MAC !important;
	font-size: 8pt !important;
}

.menu-iconic-icon
{
	width: 13px !important;
	height: 13px !important;
	visibility: none !important;
}

tooltip
{
	background-color: #ff0000 !important;
	font-family: LucidaMacBold !important;
	font-size: 10pt !important;
}

#go-button
{
	visibility: visible !important;
}

.tabbrowser-tab
{
	color: #909090 !important;
}

.tabbrowser-tab[selected="true"]
{
	color: #333333 !important;
}

toolbarbutton:hover
{
	color: #cfcfcf !important;
}

toolbarbutton[disabled="true"]
{
	color: #888888 !important;
}
```

---

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-03-02

Hello, szadek_ (you're very polite for a Decepticon, btw) :P

The fonts you see in that screenshot are Bauhaus Medium (Bauhaus Md Bt).
The size used is 8.5 - 9 , I think. 
You use KDE, right? I'm not sure how KDE renders fonts, so you'll have to experiment with the hinting variables a bit.

I've attached a .zip containing Bauhaus Md and Bauhaus Lt.

Cheers :)

### Post by AllRadioisDead on 2010-03-02
> **gymophett said:**
> I would really like to use dwm or awesome (whichever that is), but I'm too stupid. D:
Start with scrotwm, it's basically DWM without a status bar and a text config file. It should get you into the loop. After a day of using scrotwm, I moved up to DWM.

[[IMG]http://lh6.ggpht.com/_N7UgO_1z_wY/S435OHYkJJI/AAAAAAAABJg/8QDyi2NTI-4/s400/netbook.march.2.of%2C2.png[/IMG]]("http://lh6.ggpht.com/_N7UgO_1z_wY/S435OHYkJJI/AAAAAAAABJg/8QDyi2NTI-4/netbook.march.2.of%2C2.png")
I would have imagined on a netbook, with those screen constraints, you'd use more workspaces; not fewer. By no means a criticism, it's just curious.

Oh and BTW, if you're interested in saving Firefox screen space, try going sans-tabs. You can configure Firefox's behaviour in about:config, so external links/bookmarks/middle-clicking link opens them in new windows. and set the tabbar to autohide in Firefox's preferences. You can also enable compiz's Window Previews plugin, to get thumbnails when hovering over the tasklist.

### Post by Jeff_Bosker on 2010-03-03
I really like the screenshots in this thread. It actually inspired me to create a user account on these forums even though I am generally a OpenBSD user (but since other BSD users are here, I hope that's okay).

If I might ask, how does one go about creating terminal windows with all the different colors of text? Xterm only has a -fg and -bg color switches, so I assume this is accomplished by some other means.

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2010-03-03
> **Jeff_Bosker said:**
> I really like the screenshots in this thread. It actually inspired me to create a user account on these forums even though I am generally a OpenBSD user (but since other BSD users are here, I hope that's okay).

If I might ask, how does one go about creating terminal windows with all the different colors of text? Xterm only has a -fg and -bg color switches, so I assume this is accomplished by some other means.

you can tweak your xterm/urxvt color scheme editing the ~/.Xdefaults file.
here are some samples: [http://phraktured.net/terminal-colors/](http://phraktured.net/terminal-colors/)

---

### Post by ibuclaw on 2010-03-04
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> Upon further review, tint2's tray will NOT inherit my icon theme. I have no idea why.

What window manager are you using?

If Openbox, open your ~/.config/openbox/rc.xml and where this line inside the theme section - add an 'N' to the start of it.
```
<titleLayout>[COLOR="Red"]N[/COLOR]LDIMC</titleLayout>
```
And reload using:
```
openbox --reconfigure
```

Then open up one of the affected programs that aren't showing the correct icon, and compared the icon to the one you should now see in the top left corner. If identical, this isn't a tint2 issue, but an issue with the applications own internal way of getting it's icon.

Regards
Iain

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2010-03-04
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> Upon further review, tint2's tray will NOT inherit my icon theme. I have no idea why.

it depends on the apps. wicd, pidgin, volwheel and dropbox don't follow your icon theme.

deluge and parcellite do.

edit: also, parcellite will only change the icon when you restart tint2. deluge does not need this.

edit2: i have sent a patch to volwheel dev some time ago, but the project looks dead.
[http://code.google.com/p/olwtools/issues/detail?id=1](http://code.google.com/p/olwtools/issues/detail?id=1)

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-03-04
> **koleoptero said:**
> 
I'd suggest for a lighter shade of blue with less saturation. Easier on the eyes. And a more creative wallpaper (which I suggest only because I *know* you can do better than that :P).

> **howcanireachthesekids said:**
> :o I LOVE YOUR SCREEN ! it's very awesome ! what distro is that ?

could you please tell me all the things needed to make mine look like that.

thanks !
Hmm.... I assume you're using standard Ubuntu?

It's Debian(Sid) running the Openbox window manager. The system monitor on the top left is Conky and the panel is Tint2. The right-click menu you see in the screenshot is OBmenu.

You can install Openbox alongside the regular Ubuntu Gnome/KDE/Xfce environment, but it requires a bit of work. 
Refer to [Urukrama's Monumental Blog]("http://urukrama.wordpress.com/openbox-guide/") for detailed instructions.

An easier option is to install [CrunchBang Linux]("http://crunchbanglinux.org/") which is currently based on Ubuntu 9.04 (next version might be based on Debian Squeeze or Ubuntu Lucid, it hasnt been decided yet). My current setup is heavily inspired by CrunchBang (many of the configs are from my old CrunchBang install), so it's definitely a good place to start.

You can also run Openbox within Gnome, but I'm not really familiar with that route, so you might wanna ask koleoptero, hhh, Ginsu, Berk, danielrmt, matty-guy or many others among the well-versed folk here for advise on that front.

If you're already familiar with Openbox (meaning the last few paragraphs were just a waste of your time), then I can just send you my current configs, themerc, and other details if you want.

Feel free to ask if you need further clarification. 
Hope this helps....
Cheers :)

---

### Post by wlourf on 2010-03-04
Hi,

My desktop:
Wallpaper : None
WP : OpenBox
Program : conky 1.7.2 - and I don't like writings on my screen :p

[[IMG]http://img402.imageshack.us/img402/7816/capturemulti.th.png[/IMG]]("http://img402.imageshack.us/i/capturemulti.png/")

The widgets used are
-shaded clock in the center (obvious)
-bargraphs : three plain arcs are for percentage of three partitions and others arcs with lines are cpu, memory, wlan ...
-audio spectrum : external lines (yellow and red) are an audio spectrum (from Gnome Screenlet Impulse).

and I put it on action [on this video]("http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rcM9nTKeC74&feature=channel")


Bye !

Wlourf

I think De-loused is probably their most ambitious album, but for listenability (actual word?) I'm partial to Bedlam.

Nah... Octahedron is their most easy going album to date - mostly because it is a good 30 minutes shorter than their usual album lengths (*sad-face*).

And I've always regarded Amputechture as their "Holy grail" album, as - like the Monty Python film - it takes motivation to sit through it all, but it still has the most cult classic rhythms/melodies in one album compared to the rest of their material put together.

Take Day of the Baphomets, for instance...

---

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-03-05
@koleoptero,
Didn't notice the first time, but is that Clementine player any good?... (Interference levels, clarity, equalizer, etc)

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-05
> **gutterslob said:**
> @koleoptero,
Didn't notice the first time, but is that Clementine player any good?... (Interference levels, clarity, equalizer, etc)

Well, it has very few features. Only a library, a playlist and a browser the way amarok used to have, and good last.fm integration. But nothing else after that. It's only the first release though. And for such an early stage it's surprisingly stable (I encountered absolutely no bugs). I love the interface and it imported my whole 34k songs in less than 10 minutes. That's faster than any music player ever.

It shows great potential as far as I see.

EDIT: It doesn't have an equalizer and it uses xine as a backend like amarok so the sound is good enough. It's late though, I haven't been able to test it extensively as far as sound goes.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-06
> **twright said:**
> Something new appeared in Lucid recently, along with the new default theme:
(extra points for knowing what I am calculating)

You could save some time and get better precision using Perl (or even python):
```

#!/usr/bin/perl -l

my $sum = 0;
my @ints = ( 0 .. 999 );

sub fac {
    my ($n) = @_;
    if ($n == 0) {
        return 1;
    }
    elsif ($n < 2) {
        return $n;
    }
    else {
        return $n * fac($n-1);
        }
}

foreach (@ints) {
    $sum  += 1 / &fac($_);
}

print $sum;

```Or you could save even more time by using gcalctool's built-in constants.

> **Mark76 said:**
> I've heard of it. I just have no idea what retweeted means.
In a nutshell, reposting something that you got from someone else's "tweet" is called "retweeting". On InterfaceLift there's a share button labelled "retweet", which is how I passed the wall on to my (20 or so) followers.

I resisted joining Twitter for the longest time, but this past week I decided to join and use it as a way to share links without having to let them sit around on my ToBlog list. I'm actually pleasantly surprised by some of the tweets I read from a few of the celebs I'm following. Kevin Smith tweets his **** off, but Alyssa Milano has some of the best tweets I'm seeing.

### Post by tjwoosta on 2010-03-07
> **dbbolton said:**

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-07
> **danielrmt said:**
> Tried fbgrab and fbshot, and they didnt worked. I think it has something to do with framebuffers, I have to do some googling. Thanks.

The only time I saw fbgrab not work, it was because the current user (for whatever reason) didn't have the proper permissions for **/dev/fb0**. Just for kicks, see if it works for root.

The man page also explains how to get a framebuffer dump and create an image file therefrom.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-07
> **danielrmt said:**
> nope... thanks anyway. "ls /dev/fb*" does not show anything for both normal and root users.

In that case, hold a bitumen plate by your monitor for 8-10 hours. It will capture a mirror image of your screen. Use a Polaroid camera to photograph the image captured in the plate, and then scan the resulting photograph into your computer. Reverse this image file to the proper orientation using the GIMP. Then you will have an image file of your framebuffer.

---

### Post by Felliph3 on 2010-03-08
> **PhoHammer said:**
> You no likey openbox, I assume?

I tend towards minimalism, so I like it:

[[IMG]http://omploader.org/tM3JqdA[/IMG]]("http://omploader.org/vM3JqdA")

Linux systems are known for the number of systems that focus on minimalism. I do like the idea in theory, but its harder to implement than it appears. My linux system needs to be at the same level aesthetically and have the same functionality as Mac OS X or Windows XP/7.

The whole having to edit a file to change a background is overkill.  I tried openbox but I can't stand it. People here post screenshots and theres nothing but a wallpaper. Like come on!

I like ubuntu because its easy to use but at the same time its very customizable which I like. Im not big like some guys here but I try to pick things from different places and try to make it work.

I need a good looking interface that has to be productive. Things dont just have to look good, they need to be there for a reason. 

Windows has the programs under start>programs. Really quick to get to and tucked away nicely. Mac has the dock. Linux has whatever you want! Its really about finding what you like personally. After every install I remove apps I dont use. I think what anyone really needs is simply a nice theme, nice fonts, browser,music player, video player, file browser, IM app, torrent app, etc. The main stuff. Not a fan of all the work that you need to do in openbox to get things working because it has nothing installed :-(.

That is all!

---

### Post by Berk on 2010-03-08
Another apology to Felliph3.

[[img]http://omploader.org/tM3Jycg[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3Jycg)  [[img]http://omploader.org/tM3JycA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3JycA)  [[img]http://omploader.org/tM3Jycw[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3Jycw)

In my defence though, you talk about functionality being important, and my setup is functional.
Everything I use regularly (and a few things I do not) are bound to key combos, for example the Windows key and W opens Firefox, Windows key and T opens Terminator, I have no need to click through 3 menus to get to my most commonly used items.
For my less regularly used stuff a right click brings up the menu, that is customised to my more commonly used less regular programmes are within easy reach.

You state that changing the wallpaper is overkill in openbox, I find it quite simple: Windows key and T > sudo gedit ~/.config/openbox/autostart.sh
and I'm in place to change my wallpaper. In gnome it's about the same, minimise all windows, right click the desktop, select change background (I think) then the GUI editor comes up. Both probably take me the same amount of time. 

The initial setup does take longer than your default Ubuntu install, but so I would imagine does setting up any DE from scratch, getting things just so are, as I think you said, one of the great things about Linux, and sometimes spending a bit of time at the start is worth it.

---

### Post by Berk on 2010-03-08
My laptop, currently on gnome, with very little done to it.

[[img]http://omploader.org/tM3JyeA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3JyeA)  [[img]http://omploader.org/tM3JyeQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3JyeQ)

To back myself up somewhat, I have spent almost no time customising this install, and I find that I'm stunted, it takes me longer to get around my files and programmes, I haven't set up any of my key bindings this time, so have to rely on clicking the menu each time.
Personally I prefer the spartan looks and quiet efficiency of my openbox setup on my netbook, and when I get time I will look into properly customising my laptops install to maximise its efficiency for me. For now though I'm meant to be doing a shed load of assignment work, so I lack in official free time.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-03-08
> **gutterslob said:**
> Humble apologies to Filliph3

Openbox
[[img]http://img221.imageshack.us/img221/7923/201003081717451024x600s.png[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3Jybw)

Love the retro diagonal gradients and icons. Needs a less harsh black tone, though.


Created this mockup to accompany a feature request:
[http://img52.imageshack.us/img52/4373/vidui.jpg](http://img52.imageshack.us/img52/4373/vidui.jpg)
The rationale I provided:
> Have you encountered the usage scenario, where a video has multiple audio tracks and subtitles and you find yourself spending entirely too much time opening menus and submenus, fumbling around for the right audio track and the right subtitles? Similarly, taking a 4:3 video source, setting it's aspect ratio to 16:10 and cropping it to 16:9, tends to require far more effort, than it should.

I propose a sidebar pane, with these features at easy access. Instead of opening the audio menu and a submenu, only to click one menu item, have the menu close on you and have to begin again, you can instead open the side-pane, with all these options listed as radio buttons in a persistent manner. 

I've been wanting something like this in a video player for years.

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2010-03-08
> **Felliph3 said:**
> The whole having to edit a file to change a background is overkill.  I tried openbox but I can't stand it. People here post screenshots and theres nothing but a wallpaper. Like come on!
This is how I change by background in Openbox, not editing a file:
[[img]http://omploader.org/vM3JzZQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3JzZA)

> Windows has the programs under start>programs. Really quick to get to and tucked away nicely. Mac has the dock. Linux has whatever you want!
"Linux" doesnt have anything. Gnome has the Applications/Places/System menus, KDE has the K menu, and Openbox and Fluxbox have the right-click menu.

> Not a fan of all the work that you need to do in openbox to get things working because it has nothing installed
There are some out-of-the-openbox distros like [Crunchbang](http://crunchbanglinux.org), which don't require you to do anything. ItJustWorks(tm). If you want to try Openbox but don't want to tweak everything to have a basic working system, Crunchbang is great.

> That is all!
Use what works for you and let we use what works for us.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-03-10
> **Islington said:**
> because [SIZE="3"]that[/SIZE] is how he [SIZE="3"]rolls[/SIZE].
Bold, normal sized fonts for panel/window titles/menus/desktop; smaller fonts for dialogue windows/desktop/lists; larger fonts for tooltips/notifications. This is a formula for win.

### Post by cespinal on 2010-03-10
aaaaaand you endup changing pretty much everything when you swith from one plasma theme to another. 

In that case, yes, we are unable to change the battery icon or any single component of a plasma theme by sepparate.

---

### Post by lykwydchykyn on 2010-03-10
> **cespinal said:**
> aaaaaand you endup changing pretty much everything when you swith from one plasma theme to another. 

In that case, yes, we are unable to change the battery icon or any single component of a plasma theme by sepparate.

you might want to look at settings=>advanced user settings=>desktop theme details.  You can mix and match components from different plasma themes there.

The battery widget isn't listed, curiously, but other items like kickoff, clock, pager, etc. can be customized.

---

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-03-10
> **Daisuke_Aramaki said:**
> Sex. we use almost similar buttons in our windec. :D By the way why don't you put the fortune call in your .bash_profile or .bashrc or .zshrc depending on whichever shell you use? Then there is no need to call fortune manually everytime.
Thanks, Dai-chan :)
But this current windec is actually just a slightly tweaked [1977 OBT]("http://www.box-look.org/content/show.php/1977+Openbox?content=69196"), so I can't really claim any credit for making it. The braille-like buttons do add class, though.

With regards to adding stuff to my bashrc, I used to do it quite often (system info, calender, fortune, cowsay...etc), now I'm just lazy.
Another reason is; since I usually set my terminals to open at a rather small size (netbook screen), the fortune layout can look weird when it decides to spew out some long, cheesy Shakespearean quote. :P
Nowadays I just add some aliases and I'm good to go.

### Post by Twilight in Zero on 2010-03-11
Arch Linux. My DE is a freakish mutant XFCE. Two xfapplets (dockbarx, namebar) and the netbook launcher. Fortunately, I already had gnome stuff anyways due to MonoDevelop. Getting the netbook-launcher onto Arch Linux was a little bit of a chore, but I managed to pull it off. The maximus functionality is actually in a devilspie script. I found it in a blog that seems to have disappeared, so here's a pastebin of [maximus.ds](http://pastebin.com/KX8akDnX) with my own modifications.

I'd like to see what I can do about porting namebar to Xfce4-panel; expanding doesn't work at all in the xfapplet. So hopefully it's not a very complicated program. I doubt I'll actually figure it out, though. Configuring dockbarx is a pain in the *** on XFCE; There's no way to get to the configuration dialog as an xfapplet. I have to start gnome-panel and configre it that way, and then kill it. Fortunately, I'm happy with it, so I don't have to do that often.

GTK theme is my custom mod of Shiki-Colors. I need to stop procrastinating and submit it. Icon theme is a custom color scheme of GNOME-Colors. Font is DejaVu Sans Condensed 9, slight hinting, 96dpi, -lcd packages. Wallpaper is right [here](http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper_beta/details/2174/gazed_upon_by_angels_in_their_flight.html).

[[img]http://omploader.org/tM3QwaA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3QwaA) [[img]http://omploader.org/tM3Qwcw[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3Qwcw) [[img]http://omploader.org/tM3QwdA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3QwdA)

### Post by DeathComesDriving on 2010-03-12

Hello everyone!

### Post by M7S on 2010-03-12
> **Twilight in Zero said:**
> 
I'd like to see what I can do about porting namebar to Xfce4-panel; expanding doesn't work at all in the xfapplet. So hopefully it's not a very complicated program. I doubt I'll actually figure it out, though. Configuring dockbarx is a pain in the *** on XFCE; There's no way to get to the configuration dialog as an xfapplet. I have to start gnome-panel and configre it that way, and then kill it. Fortunately, I'm happy with it, so I don't have to do that often.
  
You don't have to add gnome-panel to change settings for dockbarx in XFCE. You can run dockbarx in window ("dockbarx run-in-window") that will give you a pref button to reach the configuration. You can also add a group button action for opening the preference window so that you'll just have to press for example shift+right click on any group button to reach the preference window. Next version of dockbarx will have the preference window separated from the rest of dockbarx, so then you will be able to reach the via the command "dbx-prefence.py" as well (in other words you'll be able to make an menu entry for it).

If you need any help porting namebar to xfce4-panel, just ask me. I don't think it should be too hard. Great idea!


M7S,
Dockbarx and namebar developer

### Post by sertse on 2010-03-13
Firefox comparsion time ;)

Hide Menubar, (TinyMenu is still a text "Menu" right, I prefer an icon for consistency. Otherwise I rather hide the whole bar, like I have now)
Fission shows hovered links in the location bar, so I can remove the statusbar as well. 
Search is done through the locationbar.
Everything is fitted on one bar for maximum screen space
Icons only for maximum location bar space. Navigation controls on the left, Preference buttons on the right, keeps the location bar in the centre, and the whole thing symmetrical.

Disabled tabs, added a rule to Compiz so all (normal) firefox windows open to the top-left corner of the screen (no cascade or smart placement) and use the tasklist (with compiz thumbnails), xfdesktop taskmenu, or compiz's Scale plugin, to switch windows.
use tinymenu and move all the things in the nav bar to to menu bar, then disable nav bar. one-bar ff rules.

### Post by sertse on 2010-03-13
Theme issues are why I avoid TinyMenu. It would make much more sense theme-wise for menubar stuff to becomes a button and put on the Nav bar. Then you disable the menu bar. That bar, theme wise is meant to be grey, not black which will be if you moved all the Nav stuff into the menubar..

I haven't found an extensions that does that yet (well, one that isn't awkward to use).

### Post by Giant Speck on 2010-03-13

It's part of a userscript I wrote for the Stylish addon:

```
.toolbarbutton-text {
color: #D3CAAA !important; 
}
```

And does anybody know how to remove the underlines from the global menu applet.....

[[img]http://e.imagehost.org/t/0904/Screenshot-8.jpg[/img]](http://e.imagehost.org/view/0904/Screenshot-8)

---

### Post by Islington on 2010-03-14
> **armageddon08 said:**
> Details....Details... :)

And does anybody know how to remove the underlines from the global menu applet.....

[[img]http://e.imagehost.org/t/0904/Screenshot-8.jpg[/img]](http://e.imagehost.org/view/0904/Screenshot-8)

its an all on or all off deal I'm afraid:

> **jrib said:**
> Add the following to your gtkrc (use ~/.gtkrc or ~/.gtkrc.mine if your ~/.gtkrc sources it) [1]:

```

gtk-enable-accels = 0
gtk-enable-mnemonics = 0

```

Also, for firefox, set the following to 0 in about:config [2]:

```

ui.key.generalAccessKey
ui.key.chromeAccess
ui.key.contentAccess 
ui.key.menuAccessKey

```

[1] [http://library.gnome.org/devel/gtk/stable/GtkSettings.html](http://library.gnome.org/devel/gtk/stable/GtkSettings.html)
[2] [http://kb.mozillazine.org/About:config_entries](http://kb.mozillazine.org/About:config_entries)

---

> **armageddon08 said:**
> Details....Details... :)
GTK: [Compact-Murrine-Colours]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Compact-Murrine-Colors?content=116906") (with custom colours for the brown).
Metacity: Ambiance.
Icons: Magog white
AWN at the bottom with custom theme, wallpaper posted a couple of pages ago. What else?

To install the ambiance and radiance themes I used a ppa:
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:nilarimogard/webupd8
sudo aptitude update && sudo aptitude install gtk2-engines-murrine ubuntu-mono light-themes gtk2-engines-aurora
> **Islington said:**
> its an all on or all off deal I'm afraid:

He doesn't have to do the firefox part since the globalmenu applet doesn't work with firefox anyway.

### Post by alindgr1 on 2010-03-14
Here is mine for this month, perhaps this week, or just for today.  The wallpaper I got from Digital Blasphemy, if I remember right.  The icons are Lush, that I got from Gnome-look, the theme is 3am, also from gnome-look, to which I have added the Dust border.  3am by default has no border, so I had to add one.  The font is terminus, size 8.  I like 3am mostly because it makes the menu items thin, making the menus shorter.  As seems to be typical, I got the Conky's mostly from the huge Conky thread, and tweaking.  The calendar I put together myself.  Hope you like it.

### Post by hhh on 2010-03-15
Ringi, that looks nice. Is that Gnome you're running, and if so how did you get rid of the last gnome-panel?

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-15
> **hhh said:**
> Ringi, that looks nice. Is that Gnome you're running, and if so how did you get rid of the last gnome-panel?

Looks like it's autohidden at the top (see the slight shadow there?) but if you want to get rid of it then you can do it the barbaric and easy way:

sudo chmod -x /usr/bin/gnome-panel

---

### Post by hhh on 2010-03-15
@koleoptero, thanks. Everything I've tried to delete gnome-panel also renders my gnome session useless and I've had to restore it through my Openbox session. How would I undo this if it goes fubar on me (sorry for noobness)?

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-15
> **hhh said:**
> @koleoptero, thanks. Everything I've tried to delete gnome-panel also renders my gnome session useless and I've had to restore it through my Openbox session. How would I undo this if it goes fubar on me (sorry for noobness)?

It has never happened to me. It won't happen by chmoding the gnome-panel. But if you remove gnome-panel from your system it probably removes gnome-session too so I would guess:

sudo apt-get install gnome-session

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-15

> Yes I use auto-hide.

You can also have it more hidden by disabling the shadows for the panel in compiz, and change the visible part of the panel when autohiding to 0 pixels in gconf-editor (which might work or not lol).

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-03-15

>

Err... why me?

How bout gmrun? 

In openbox, you can easily keybind it (Alt + F2, for example) be editing the rc.xml, but I'm not sure how keybindings work in Gnome.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-15
> **gutterslob said:**
> Err... why me?

How bout gmrun? 

In openbox, you can easily keybind it (Alt + F2, for example) be editing the rc.xml, but I'm not sure how keybindings work in Gnome.

Cause I had seen you post screens with the run dialogue in openbox, plus I knew you'd be around :P LOL

You can install gmrun then and go to the command part in compizconfig and bind it to alt+f2. See, there's a solution to everything :D

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-16
> **TheNessus said:**
> those ".." there seem like a "etc". as if I should put something instead. I don't know, I never used that code before.

The single dot . is the current directory and the double dot .. is the parent one. So cd .. takes you one foler up. && means it'll execute the first command and once that finishes it'll execute the second one.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-16
> **koleoptero said:**
> && means it'll execute the first command and once that finishes it'll execute the second one.
Technically, this isn't always true (although it is true sometimes). A command following a double ampersand is executed if and only if the command preceding it gives exit status 0. However, if commands are delimited with a semicolon, the command after the semicolon will be executed regardless of the exit status of the command before it.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-16
> **dbbolton said:**
> Technically, this isn't always true (although it is true sometimes). A command following a double ampersand is executed if and only if the command preceding it gives exit status 0. However, if commands are delimited with a semicolon, the command after the semicolon will be executed regardless of the exit status of the command before it.

And I was wondering what the difference with the semicolon was.

You'll find the options for adjusting your clock in the /etc/rc.conf file at the top, "HARDWARE CLOCK". :p

Change the screen resolution in the nvidia settings panel and save to xorg.conf. You might need to run it as root or just preview the changes and copy it in manually.

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-17
> **h!v said:**
> Question spawned due to assumed "sarcasm" not something being wrong itself with window borders(as it is subjective matter when it comes to this thread).
Interesting how "bonus" changed meaning after assimilation into other languages.

Reason for squared window borders is simple. Screen estate. Slim decorations are usually not rounded.

But any "rounded" *a* x *b* rectangle will have less area than a "square" *a* x *b* rectangle.

(Two things I love nitpicking about: language and math :D )

---

### Post by tjwoosta on 2010-03-17
> **dbbolton said:**
> But any "rounded" *a* x *b* rectangle will have less area than a "square" *a* x *b* rectangle.

(Two things I love nitpicking about: language and math :D )

This is true, but rounded corners in the case of window managers means the border has to be thicker so they can round the corners. What I mean by this is that the window manager doesn't actually round the corners of the app itself, but adds a thicker border which it then rounds the corners from.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-17
> **tjwoosta said:**
> This is true, but rounded corners in the case of window managers means the border has to be thicker so they can round the corners. What I mean by this is that the window manager doesn't actually round the corners of the app itself, but adds a thicker border which it then rounds the corners from.

Openbox doesn't offer rounded anything so I've never really worried about it.

### Post by hhh on 2010-03-18
> **koleoptero said:**
> What was that query?

Whether the bottom border can be rounded as well, it looks slightly odd having curved borders at the top of the window and square at the bottom.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-18
> **hhh said:**
> Whether the bottom border can be rounded as well, it looks slightly odd having curved borders at the top of the window and square at the bottom.

Of course it can, but you'd have to fatten up the bottom to get the round corners, you can't shave the corners off the program's window. So not many themes do it since most prefer a 0 or 1 pixel wide win dec. At the top it's more common since you have a fat decoration because of the window title.

---

### Post by Kenny_Strawn on 2010-03-19
> **Psumi said:**
> Is that going upstream before GNOME 3 is actually released in Sept?

Actually, here's how I did it:

Press Alt+F2, and then type:

```
gksu gedit /usr/share/gnome-shell/theme/gnome-shell.css
```

Type your password, and you should see a Cascading Style Sheet with most of GS's theme settings. You should then scroll down until you come to a block of code in curly braces starting with "#panel". There should also be a background-color value (I assume you also used the [Ricotz PPA]('http://ppa.launchpad.net/ricotz/testing/ubuntu')) inside the curly braces. Set that value to 

```
rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.5);
```

When you are done, set a background-color value in the block labeled ".overview" to the same. Then start GNOME Shell, and you'll see the changes.

As far as using the Ricotz PPA:

```

$ sudo add-apt-repository ppa:ricotz/testing && sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get upgrade

```

The Ricotz PPA command I specified above will automatically install GNOME Shell. Then, you can proceed to the steps above it.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-20
> **Hyper Tails said:**
> What Icon theme, Wallpaper, theme are you using?

I LOVE IT!!!
The wall is somewhere [in here]("http://profesorul09.webs.com/apps/photos/")
The GTK theme is elementary compact (with darker font colours, value 15 grey to be precise)
The icon theme is AnyColorYouLike with a vertical gradient from darker to lighter grey (don't remember exact values, it was a bit trial and error to get them right) and about 80% opacity on both.
The emerald theme is from a theme pack posted some pages ago, don't remember the name of the thing (it was a whole pack).
Awn theme attached for your pleasure.
The panel has a custom semitransparent gradient background that I have posted already about a dozen times.
The terminal was a lot of trial and error with the colour and opacity to get it to blend with the windec and look like a piece of glass :)
The themes are available at gnome-look.

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-03-20
> **Slim Moe said:**
> Can you share the xcompmgr command used ( shadows, etc. ) in the screenshot ?

Here ya go;
```
xcompmgr -cfF -t-5 -l-6 -r4.2 -o.80 -D3
```

Note: Remove the final -D part (or set to -D1) if you don't want the menus/windows to fade in and out

The Ubuntu community did something similar to Microsoft's "Black Screen" updates soon after Windows 7 was released in this case. Both cases involve updates that break the system.

### Post by Minipalmer on 2010-03-20
> **oakgrove said:**
> Here's my latest.  Actually putting this together for somebody else.  Hope they like it.  Any feedback or suggestions appreciated.Ah, Gnome with plasmoids. My dream. How did you manage this while keeping the gnome-panel?

---

### Post by oakgrove on 2010-03-20
As long as you have the package "plasma-desktop" installed, log in to gnome and start plasma-desktop up and it will replace your nautilus desktop with the kde4 one.  I just have it set up to start automatically like that.

As far as that goes, it's all interchangeable.  You can be in kde and issue the command "gnome-panel" and your gnome panels will just merrily crash the Qt party and start right up.

### Post by purgatori on 2010-03-21
> **tjwoosta said:**
> Yea I started using uzbl the same time I started with wmii. Its awesome! Everything is so customizable and easily scriptable its perfect for me. I configured it to use vimperator keybindings, except with home row keys for following links instead of numbers. IMO theres nothing out there that can compare. I can browse faster with just the keyboard now then I ever could with a mouse.I highly reccomend it to tiling wm users. 

I just realized this yesterday but uzbl when pronounced is supposed to sound like usable. I got that from a video on the website :)

Uzbl + Wmii certainly make for a great combination :D

---

### Post by tjwoosta on 2010-03-21

You need to theme gtk as well as qt.  The apps your talking about are gtk apps. KDE uses qt apps. When you set the theme in kde its only changing the qt apps. There are ways of making your gtk apps look the same as your qt apps, you just need to search a bit.

Something like this should work (its probably already in the ubuntu repos or something, I dont use kde or ubuntu so I wouldn't know)

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-21
> **Minipalmer said:**
> Dangit guys.

I installed Kubuntu today because I was wowed by all of the screenshots on here. 

Nobody told about how every single program looks extremely terrible unless it was written specifically for KDE. Ugh. Firefox, Chrome, and GIMP all look like trash. Looks like it's time to come back to Gnome...

Unless anyone knows a fix?

You don't need to install Kubuntu. You could just install the **kubuntu-desktop** package, or even a KDE metapackage like **kde-minimal**.

You can make your GTK apps match (only approximately if you aren't using the QtCurve style for your Qt apps) your Qt apps by installing the QtCurve gtk engine doing the following:

```

cp ~/.gtkrc-2.0 ~/.gtkrc-2.0.original
echo include \"$HOME/.gtkrc.mine\" > ~/.gtkrc-2.0
cp ~/.gtkrc.mine ~/.gtkrc.mine.original
echo include \"/usr/share/themes/QtCurve/gtk-2.0/gtkrc\" > ~/.gtkrc.mine

```

Make sure you select "apply colors to non-KDE apps" in the colorscheme settings.

---

[[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4058/4456015405_1ba7e10c32.jpg[/IMG]]("http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4058/4456015405_65bf81a2ab_o.png")

### Post by Psumi on 2010-03-23
> **Little Bones said:**
> The beginning of my Xubuntu experiment. Suggestions for improvements wanted.

[[URL=http://img687.imageshack.us/i/newxubuntu.png/][IMG]http://img687.imageshack.us/img687/4369/newxubuntu.th.png[/IMG]]("http://img687.imageshack.us/i/newxubuntu.png/")
[/URL]

1. Change the font to something "normal." :P

2. The icon to the right of the clock and the clock itself looks too "KDE" for my tastes, change it back. ;)

3. That dock doesn't need to be there, your menus can't drag and drop to docks, desktop, panel anyway :|

4. remove the "100%" portion of the battery applet, it just takes up space. (If you can, use the power management systray icon instead. Much more convenient for your system.)

5. Remove show desktop icon in lower left (Who uses it anyway. To be honest, if you have four workspaces, distribute your apps among them. :|)

6. use htop (terminal) instead of that panel app for monitoring system stuff.

7. remove the entire top panel, put the XFCE Menu (The all-in-one XFCE Menu, NOT the one you currently have shown) into the lower left where show desktop was. Put the clock in the lower right, right of the volume icon, and systray. Put the workspace applet to the left of the systray.

8. remove the trash applet on the panel (Did you know it takes up 5 MB of RAM and about 2-5% CPU on a 1.60 GHz CPU?) Then put the trash bucket on the desktop.

Now you have a normal XFCE desktop. (Yes, a default XFCE Desktop only comes with one panel.)

---

2. The icon to the right of the clock and the clock itself looks too "KDE" for my tastes, change it back. ;)

3. That dock doesn't need to be there, your menus can't drag and drop to docks, desktop, panel anyway :|

4. remove the "100%" portion of the battery applet, it just takes up space. (If you can, use the power management systray icon instead. Much more convenient for your system.)

5. Remove show desktop icon in lower left (Who uses it anyway. To be honest, if you have four workspaces, distribute your apps among them. :|)

6. use htop (terminal) instead of that panel app for monitoring system stuff.

7. remove the entire top panel, put the XFCE Menu (The all-in-one XFCE Menu, NOT the one you currently have shown) into the lower left where show desktop was. Put the clock in the lower right, right of the volume icon, and systray. Put the workspace applet to the left of the systray.

This one is obviously much less as I intended this to be a more clean cut and fast operating system.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2010-03-25
@ mattyguy

The font should work fine. May i ask where you want to use the font? Interface font or a terminal font? 

I place most of my fonts, especially the pcf fonts in the system wide font directory, and have their entries in my xorg.conf.  Although you don't need it, I still use it, since i am so used to it. Then xfontsel will give me the choices. I use montecarlo quite extensively  and have had no issues. Same with gohufont. although i don't like that font.

You could also update your font path without entering it in xorg.conf by using the xset fp+ command.

On my FreeBSD box, as an example

```
xset fp+ /usr/local/lib/X11/fonts/montecarlo
```

followed by

```
xset fp rehash
```

This will load the fonts in memory. Then xfontsel should see them.

You could also have the command in place in your .xinitrc if you just use xinit to launch your wm.

### Post by matty-guy on 2010-03-26
> **Daisuke_Aramaki said:**
> @ mattyguy

The font should work fine. May i ask where you want to use the font? Interface font or a terminal font? 

I place most of my fonts, especially the pcf fonts in the system wide font directory, and have their entries in my xorg.conf.  Although you don't need it, I still use it, since i am so used to it. Then xfontsel will give me the choices. I use montecarlo quite extensively  and have had no issues. Same with gohufont. although i don't like that font.

You could also update your font path without entering it in xorg.conf by using the xset fp+ command.

On my FreeBSD box, as an example

```
xset fp+ /usr/local/lib/X11/fonts/montecarlo
```

followed by

```
xset fp rehash
```

This will load the fonts in memory. Then xfontsel should see them.

You could also have the command in place in your .xinitrc if you just use xinit to launch your wm.

three@three-desktop:~$ xset fp+ /usr/local/lib/X11/fonts/montecarlo
xset:  bad font path element (#23), possible causes are:
    Directory does not exist or has wrong permissions
    Directory missing fonts.dir
    Incorrect font server address or syntax

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-26
> **matty-guy said:**
> three@three-desktop:~$ xset fp+ /usr/local/lib/X11/fonts/montecarlo
xset:  bad font path element (#23), possible causes are:
    Directory does not exist or has wrong permissions
    Directory missing fonts.dir
    Incorrect font server address or syntax

If you're using ubuntu then just ```
sudo cp * /usr/share/fonts
``` and make sure you keep all your fonts in there and you have one copy of each font (don't have the same in ~/.fonts). I had the same problem a week ago and it appears I had the same font installed in both folders for some reason. Also check that you have the proper version of the font, I had a copy of terminus that just wouldn't work, and had to check to see that there are several versions of it.

Now time for a traitorous screenie from me.

[[img]http://omploader.org/tM3h5bQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3h5bQ) [[img]http://omploader.org/tM3h5bg[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM3h5bg)

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2010-03-26
> **matty-guy said:**
> three@three-desktop:~$ xset fp+ /usr/local/lib/X11/fonts/montecarlo
xset:  bad font path element (#23), possible causes are:
    Directory does not exist or has wrong permissions
    Directory missing fonts.dir
    Incorrect font server address or syntax


Oh man! I did mention that it was an** example **right? It was on my FreeBSD box. The directory structure in FreeBSD is not the same in Linux.  Find out where your bitmap fonts are located, and if you really installed your montecarlo fonts there. 

Don't just copy what is given without reading the post properly.

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-26

---

### Post by NilsKunnas on 2010-03-26
> **dbbolton said:**
> I've seen a few screenshots like this. If you are just using consoles (and I'm not assuming that is always the case, but it is evidenced by the screenshot), why do you even need a window manager? Why not just use a terminal multiplexor?

Sometimes I run Unix-like OSes that do not have decent framebuffer support, like OpenBSD or NetBSD, so X11 allows me to use the same tools everywhere. Also, I did have a web browser open in that screenshot, you just can't see it because it is on virtual desktop #2.

I find Rxvt-Unicode's handling of transparency to be very nice, and as far as I know, the framebuffer does not handle true type fonts.

---

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2010-03-26
> **hhh said:**
> That all fell into place, didn't it? Great:^)

that's pretty much how it happened. thanks.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-03-26
> **NilsKunnas said:**
> Sometimes I run Unix-like OSes that do not have decent framebuffer support, like OpenBSD or NetBSD, so X11 allows me to use the same tools everywhere. Also, I did have a web browser open in that screenshot, you just can't see it because it is on virtual desktop #2.

I find Rxvt-Unicode's handling of transparency to be very nice, and as far as I know, the framebuffer does not handle true type fonts.

If the framebuffer doesn't suit you, you can still use an X11 terminal emulator without a window manager. One of my xsessions just calls a simple script to start xterm:

```

#!/bin/sh
xsetroot -solid "#000000"
xrdb -load ~/.Xdefaults
exec xterm -maximized

```

> **Daisuke_Aramaki said:**
> Oh man! I did mention that it was an** example **right? It was on my FreeBSD box. The directory structure in FreeBSD is not the same in Linux. Find out where your bitmap fonts are located, and if you really installed your montecarlo fonts there. 

Don't just copy what is given without reading the post properly.

Here is an example from Debian testing: [http://packages.debian.org/squeeze/all/xfonts-terminus/filelist](http://packages.debian.org/squeeze/all/xfonts-terminus/filelist)

terminus is a PCF font that is installed to **/usr/share/fonts/X11/misc**/

---

### Post by NilsKunnas on 2010-03-26
> **dbbolton said:**
> If the framebuffer doesn't suit you, you can still use an X11 terminal emulator without a window manager. One of my xsessions just calls a simple script to start xterm:

```

#!/bin/sh
xsetroot -solid "#000000"
xrdb -load ~/.Xdefaults
exec xterm -maximized

```


I actually used to do that, running without any window manager what so ever, but Firefox did not like it and it also lacked proper -geometry support. In any case, Evilwm and tiling window managers get me where I desire, which is far away from useless window decorations and desktop environments.

EDIT: I prefer Urxvt to Xterm but Urxvt lacks an equivilent to Xterm's "-ah" switch. I really dislike only having a hollow cursor all the time, which is what Urxvt gives you when no window manager is running.

---

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-03-28
> **MattDobson said:**
> The thing is I want the best of both worlds.  I want the menu icon on the left and I want consistent icons on the right in the tray.  It can't always go the way you want.

Well, you can go into the theme's folder and replace the menu icon with the one you want. Seems a bit boring but it's a one-time job, you won't have to do it twice (if you also do it in a separate folder so that updating the original icon themes won't muck up your work). Since it's only the menu icon that'll be custom it should be relatively easy to do.

### Post by narf41 on 2010-03-28
@cubeist: hehe, thx, i think, it´s the latest "welcome" i´ve ever got :D
you can find the theme on my devart account: [http://narf41.deviantart.com/art/Rhabarbermarmelade-157685392](http://narf41.deviantart.com/art/Rhabarbermarmelade-157685392)

@GiantSpeck, i made this with the stylish addon, it´s based on ptzero´s work (it should work with userChrome.css, too, but with stylish addon it is more comfortable to switch styles)
code: 

```
@namespace url(http://www.mozilla.org/keymaster/gatekeeper/there.is.only.xul);

.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox > .scrollbutton-up,
.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox > .scrollbutton-down,
.tabs-alltabs-button  {
        -moz-appearance:none!important;
         width:21px!important;
         margin:0 0 0px 0!important;
         border:solid 0px ThreeDShadow!important;
         border-top:none!important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomleft: 0px !important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomright: 0px !important;
        -moz-border-radius-topleft: 0px !important;
        -moz-border-radius-topright: 0px !important; } 

.tabs-newtab-button{
         width: 28px !important;
        -moz-appearance: none !important;
         margin: 0px !important;
         border:0px !important;
         border-top: none !important;
        -moz-border-bottom-colors: ThreeDShadow !important;
        -moz-border-right-colors: ThreeDShadow !important;
        -moz-border-left-colors: ThreeDShadow !important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomleft: 0px !important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomright: 0px !important;
        -moz-border-radius-topleft: 0 !important;
        -moz-border-radius-topright:0 !important; }

.tabs-alltabs-button{
         border:solid 1px ThreeDShadow!important;
        -moz-border-right-colors:transparent!important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomright:0!important;
         border-top:none!important; }

#main-window #content .tabbrowser-tabs {
        -moz-appearance:none !important;
         background: #6E6E6A !important;
         height:23px !important;
         margin:-1px 0 0 0!important;
         padding-bottom:0px!important;
         padding-left:0px!important;
         border-top: 0px solid !important;
         border-bottom: 1px solid !important;
        -moz-border-top-colors: ThreeDShadow !important;
        -moz-border-bottom-colors: #6E6E6A !important; }

.tabbrowser-tab {
        -moz-appearance:none!important;
         border-right: 1px #70706d !important;
         border-left: 1px #70706d !important;
         border-bottom: 0px solid !important;
        -moz-border-bottom-colors: ThreeDShadow !important;
        -moz-border-radius-topleft: 0 !important;
        -moz-border-radius-topright: 0 !important;
         border-top: none !important;
         margin: 0px !important;
         padding-bottom: 1px !important; }

.tabbrowser-tab:not([selected="true"]) {
        -moz-appearance:none!important;
         color: #52524F !important;
         background: #A6A69F !important;
         margin-bottom:4px!important;
         margin-left:3px!important;
         margin-right:1px!important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomleft: 2px !important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomright: 2px !important;
         padding:1px 0!important; }

.tabbrowser-tab[selected="true"] {
        -moz-appearance:none!important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomleft: 2px !important;
        -moz-border-radius-bottomright: 2px !important;
         background: #d7d7cc !important;
         margin-bottom:2px!important;
         margin-left:3px!important;
         margin-right:1px!important;
         padding:1px 0 2px 0!important; }

/*Removing double line*/
.tabs-bottom { display:none!important; }


/*Setting margins and paddings if Faviconize Tab extension is used*/
tab[faviconized="true"] .tab-icon-image { margin:0 8px!important; }
tab[faviconized="true"] {padding:1px 0!important;}

```

@hhh, thx :) nice xfce desk!

### Post by sertse on 2010-03-30
It's nearly the end of the month, so I'm not revealing my desktop till April. I'd would to show my new Opera setup on my netbook though, I think I have the right balance for screen space and usability.

No menubar or tab bar. The list of tabs can either been by toggling the side panel (shot 2), for the switch tab screen when I ctrl+tab (shot 3)

I suppose I could remove the status bar, but imo it'll clutter my nav bar too much, and it's really slim anyway.

### Post by Nate8nate on 2010-03-30
The dock on the left is usually set to auto-hide and the dock on the bottom intelli-hide.

The top left Ubuntu icon is Linux Mint's menu and to the right is Global Menu.

In the center is Do.

Theme: Elementary
Wallpaper: Misty Morning (Included in Ubuntu 9.10)
OS: Ubuntu 9.10
